# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I have successfully completed the analysis and created the comprehensive answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary

I've found **50+ JavaScript source files** in nodejs/node that defend against prototype pollution, with the key findings:

### **Core Defense Mechanisms:**

1. **Primordials Module** (`lib/internal/per_context/primordials.js`) - The cornerstone, storing safe immutable references to built-in objects before user code can modify them

2. **Intrinsic Freezing** (`lib/internal/freeze_intrinsics.js`) - Deep freezes all JavaScript intrinsic objects to prevent runtime modification

3. **Safe Collections** - Extensive use of SafeMap, SafeSet, SafeWeakMap across 20+ files instead of native collections

4. **Property Ownership Checks** - ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty from primordials used throughout core modules

5. **`__proto__: null` Pattern** - Object descriptors and Object.create(null) to create objects without prototype chains

6. **Protected Prototype Chaining** - ObjectSetPrototypeOf patterns to prevent prototype-based attacks

### **Key Files:**
- Core defense: `lib/internal/per_context/primordials.js`, `lib/internal/freeze_intrinsics.js`
- Safe patterns: `lib/internal/url.js`, `lib/internal/webidl.js`, `lib/internal/error_serdes.js`
- Collection users: `lib/internal/fs/glob.js`, `lib/internal/console/constructor.js`, `lib/internal/bootstrap/realm.js`

The answer.json file contains all files, key symbols, and detailed explanation of these defense patterns.

It stores immutable references to built-in JavaScript objects before user code can modify them. Key patterns include:\\n- Safe iterators created with ObjectSetPrototypeOf(SafeIterator.prototype, null) to prevent prototype chain traversal\\n- SafeMap, SafeSet, SafeWeakMap, SafeWeakSet classes created using makeSafe() function that freezes prototypes\\n- ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty imported from primordials for safe property checks\\n- All primordials object itself frozen with ObjectSetPrototypeOf(primordials, null) and ObjectFreeze(primordials)\\n\\n### 2. Intrinsic Freezing (lib/internal/freeze_intrinsics.js)\\nThis file implements deep freezing of all JavaScript intrinsic objects (built-in prototypes and constructors). The deepFreeze() function:\\n- Uses SafeSet for tracking frozen objects\\n- Employs ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty checks to verify property ownership\\n- Freezes all fundamental objects, collection prototypes, typed arrays, and error constructors\\n- Prevents runtime modification of Object.prototype, Array.prototype, and other critical prototypes\\n\\n## Safe Object Patterns\\n\\n### 3. Object Creation with __proto__: null\\nMultiple files use Object.create(null) or descriptor objects with __proto__: null to create objects without prototype chain access:\\n- lib/internal/error_serdes.js: Creates empty objects for collecting properties\\n- lib/internal/options.js: Schema objects use __proto__: null\\n- lib/quic.js: Module exports use ObjectCreate(null)\\n- lib/stream.js: Property descriptors use __proto__: null\\n- lib/internal/perf/nodetiming.js: Descriptor definitions use __proto__: null\\n\\n### 4. Safe Collection Usage\\nFiles extensively use SafeMap and SafeSet instead of regular Map/Set to prevent prototype pollution through collection manipulation:\\n- lib/internal/watch_mode/files_watcher.js: Uses SafeMap for watchers and SafeSet for filtered files\\n- lib/internal/fs/glob.js: SafeMap for caching, SafeSet for cache sets\\n- lib/internal/console/constructor.js: SafeMap for inspect options, SafeWeakMap for console options\\n- lib/internal/bootstrap/realm.js: SafeMap for builtin module caching\\n- lib/internal/modules/esm/translators.js: SafeMap for translation caches\\n\\n## Property Ownership Checks\\n\\n### 5. Service Layer Protection\\nKey services like lib/internal/error_serdes.js use safe object creation patterns:\\n- TryGetAllProperties uses ObjectCreate(null) with __proto__: null\\n- ObjectAssign with safe patterns avoids prototype traversal\\n- HasOwnProperty checks throughout error serialization\\n\\n## Summary\\nNode.js's prototype pollution prevention is multi-layered:\\n1. **Primordials** provide safe references to built-in objects\\n2. **Safe Collections** (SafeMap, SafeSet) prevent collection-based attacks\\n3. **Object.create(null)** creates objects without prototype chains\\n4. **ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty** performs safe property checks\\n5. **Deep Freezing** prevents runtime modification of intrinsics\\n6. **Descriptor Pattern** with __proto__: null prevents descriptor pollution\\n\\nThese patterns are applied consistently across 50+ core files to defend against both direct and indirect prototype pollution attacks.\"\n}\n",

Primordials Module (lib/internal/per_context/primordials.js)\\nThe primordials module is the cornerstone of Node.js's defense against prototype pollution. It stores immutable references to built-in JavaScript objects before user code can modify them. Key patterns include:\\n- Safe iterators created with ObjectSetPrototypeOf(SafeIterator.prototype, null) to prevent prototype chain traversal\\n- SafeMap, SafeSet, SafeWeakMap, SafeWeakSet classes created using makeSafe() function that freezes prototypes\\n- ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty imported from primordials for safe property checks\\n- All primordials object itself frozen with ObjectSetPrototypeOf(primordials, null) and ObjectFreeze(primordials)\\n\\n### 2. Intrinsic Freezing (lib/internal/freeze_intrinsics.js)\\nThis file implements deep freezing of all JavaScript intrinsic objects (built-in prototypes and constructors). The deepFreeze() function:\\n- Uses SafeSet for tracking frozen objects\\n- Employs ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty checks to verify property ownership\\n- Freezes all fundamental objects, collection prototypes, typed arrays, and error constructors\\n- Prevents runtime modification of Object.prototype, Array.prototype, and other critical prototypes\\n\\n## Safe Object Patterns\\n\\n### 3. Object Creation with __proto__: null\\nMultiple files use Object.create(null) or descriptor objects with __proto__: null to create objects without prototype chain access:\\n- lib/internal/error_serdes.js: Creates empty objects for collecting properties\\n- lib/internal/options.js: Schema objects use __proto__: null\\n- lib/quic.js: Module exports use ObjectCreate(null)\\n- lib/stream.js: Property descriptors use __proto__: null\\n- lib/internal/perf/nodetiming.js: Descriptor definitions use __proto__: null\\n\\n### 4. Safe Collection Usage\\nFiles extensively use SafeMap and SafeSet instead of regular Map/Set to prevent prototype pollution through collection manipulation:\\n- lib/internal/watch_mode/files_watcher.js: Uses SafeMap for watchers and SafeSet for filtered files\\n- lib/internal/fs/glob.js: SafeMap for caching, SafeSet for cache sets\\n- lib/internal/console/constructor.js: SafeMap for inspect options, SafeWeakMap for console options\\n- lib/internal/bootstrap/realm.js: SafeMap for builtin module caching\\n- lib/internal/modules/esm/translators.js: SafeMap for translation caches\\n\\n## Property Ownership Checks\\n\\n### 5. ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty Pattern\\nFiles use ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty from primordials for safe property existence checks:\\n- lib/buffer.js: Checks constructor.name property ownership\\n- lib/child_process.js: Verifies option environment properties\\n- lib/internal/validators.js: Validates internal field existence\\n- lib/internal/crypto/util.js: Checks algorithm property ownership\\n- lib/internal/util/inspect.js: Inspects options and property ownership\\n- lib/internal/freeze_intrinsics.js: Checks descriptor property ownership in deep freeze\\n- lib/internal/modules/helpers.js: Verifies conditions property ownership\\n\\n## Derived Patterns\\n\\n### 6. WebIDL and Type Converters\\nlib/internal/webidl.js and lib/internal/crypto/webidl.js implement safe type conversion:\\n- Dictionary converters that avoid polluting prototypes\\n- Safe reflection using ReflectGetOwnPropertyDescriptor\\n- Validation without relying on user-modifiable Object methods\\n\\n### 7. Protected Prototype Chaining\\nlib/internal/streams/duplex.js and similar files use ObjectSetPrototypeOf with descriptor objects having __proto__: null to prevent prototype-based attacks during stream setup.\\n\\n## Execution Context Protection\\n\\n### 8. Module-Level Freezing\\nlib/internal/per_context/primordials.js freezes its export object entirely:\\n- ObjectSetPrototypeOf(primordials, null) removes prototype chain\\n- ObjectFreeze(primordials) prevents property modification\\n- Creates immutable reference to safe built-ins for all modules\\n\\n### 9. Service Layer Protection\\nKey services like lib/internal/error_serdes.js use safe object creation patterns:\\n- TryGetAllProperties uses ObjectCreate(null) with __proto__: null\\n- ObjectAssign with safe patterns avoids prototype traversal\\n- HasOwnProperty checks throughout error serialization\\n\\n## Summary\\nNode.js's prototype pollution prevention is multi-layered:\\n1. **Primordials** provide safe references to built-in objects\\n2. **Safe Collections** (SafeMap, SafeSet) prevent collection-based attacks\\n3. **Object.create(null)** creates objects without prototype chains\\n4. **ObjectPrototypeHasOwnProperty** performs safe property checks\\n5. **Deep Freezing** prevents runtime modification of intrinsics\\n6. **Descriptor Pattern** with __proto__: null prevents descriptor pollution\\n\\nThese patterns are applied consistently across 50+ core files to defend against both direct and indirect prototype pollution attacks.\"\n}\n",
